Eggeling
  1. When he (the slaughterer) announces, ‘The victim has been quieted!’ the Adhvaryu says, ‘Neshс╣нar, lead up the lady!’ The Neshс╣нr╠е leads up the (sacrificer’s) wife bearing a vessel of water for washing the feet.

Eggeling
  1. He makes her say (V─Бg . S. VI, 12), ‘Homage be to thee, O wide-stretched!’–the wide-stretched one, forsooth, is the sacrifice; for they stretch the sacrifice (over the sacrificial ground):

hence the wide-stretched one is the sacrifice. But that wife, forsooth, is the hind-part of the sacrifice, and he wants her, thus coming forward, to propitiate the sacrifice. Thereby, then, she makes amends to that sacrifice, and thus that sacrifice does not injure her: therefore she says, ‘Homage be to thee, O wide-stretched!’

Eggeling
  1. ‘Advance, unresisted!’ whereby she means to say, ‘Advance on (a way) free from injury!’ ‘Unto the rivers of ghee, along the paths of sacred truth!’ whereby she means to say, ‘Unto good.’ [V─Бj. Eggeling
  1. Thereupon the wife cleanses with the water the (openings of the) vital airs of the victim. The reason why she thus cleanses with water the (openings of the) vital airs is this: the food of the gods is living, is immortal (ambrosia) for the immortals; but in quieting and cutting up that victim they kill it. Now the vital airs are water; hence she now puts into it those vital airs, and thus that food of the gods becomes truly living, becomes immortal for the immortals.

Eggeling
  1. Then as to why it is the wife that cleanses. The wife is a woman, and from woman progeny is born here on earth; thus he causes that (creature) to be born from that woman; and therefore the wife cleanses (the victim).

Eggeling
  1. With (V─Бj. S. VI, 14) ‘Thy speech I cleanse’ she wipes the mouth; with ‘Thy breath I cleanse,’ the nostrils; with ‘Thine eye I cleanse,’ the eyes; with ‘Thine organ of hearing I cleanse,’ the

ears; with ‘Thy navel I cleanse,’ that mysterious (opening of a) vital air; or with ‘Thy sexual organ I cleanse;’ with ‘Thy hind-part I cleanse,’ that (opening of a) vital air behind. Thus she puts the vital airs into it, revives it. Thereupon, holding the legs together, (she wipes them) with ‘Thy feet I cleanse;’ for it is on its feet chat it stands firmly; she thus makes it stand (on its feet) for the sake of a firm position.

Eggeling
  1. With one half or the whole of the water that is left, he (the Adhvaryu) and the Sacrificer 4 then sprinkle it, beginning from the head; thereby they put those vital airs into it, and revive it (beginning) from that part.

Eggeling
  1. Thus, wherever they wound it, wherever they hurt it–water being a means of soothing–they soothe it by that means of soothing, water, there

they heal it with water: ‘May that become pure in thee!’ thereby they render it sacrificially pure. With ‘Auspicious be the days!’ they pour out (the remaining water) behind the victim.

Eggeling
  1. Thus, wherever they wound it, wherever they hurt it,–lest thereafter the days and nights should be inauspicious 9,–they pour out (the water) behind the victim with, ‘Auspicious be the days.’

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon they turn the victim over so as to lie on its back. He (the Adhvaryu) puts the (other) stalk of grass thereon, with, ‘O plant, protect!’ for the knife is a thunderbolt, and thus that thunderbolt, the knife, does not injure it (the victim). He then applies the edge of the knife to it (and cuts through it) with, ‘Injure it not, O blade!’ for the knife is a thunderbolt, and thus that thunderbolt, the knife, does not injure it.

Eggeling
  1. He applies that approved edge of his, for that has been made sacrificially pure by a text 10. That which is the top part of the stalk he puts in his left hand, and that which is the bottom part he takes with his right hand.

Eggeling
  1. And where he skins (the victim), and whence the blood spirts out, there he smears it (the bottom part with blood) on both ends with (V─Бj. S. VI, I6), ‘Thou art the Rakshas’ share!’ for that blood is indeed the Rakshas’ share.

Eggeling
  1. Having thrown it away (on the utkara), he treads on it with, ‘Herewith I tread down the Rakshas! herewith I drive away the Rakshas! herewith I consign the Rakshas to the

nethermost darkness!’ Thus it is by means of the sacrifice that he drives away the evil spirits, the Rakshas. And as to its being rootless and severed on both sides,–rootless, forsooth, and severed on both sides, the Rakshas moves about in the air, even as man here moves about in the air rootless and severed on both sides: therefore it (the grass-end) is rootless and severed on both sides.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon they pull out the omentum, and envelop the two spits 13 therein with, ‘May ye envelop heaven and earth with ghee!’ whereby he endows those two, heaven and earth, with strength and sap, and puts strength and sap into them; and upon those two, thus filled with sap and affording the means of subsistence, these creatures subsist.

Eggeling
  1. The two omentum-spits are made of k─Бrshmarya wood. For when the gods in the beginning seized (slew) a victim, then, as it was drawn upwards, its sacrificial essence 14 flowed downwards, and from it sprang a tree; and because it flowed down from the (victim) as it was drawn (karsh) upwards, therefore (it became) a k─Бrshmarya tree 15. With that

same sacrificial essence he now perfects it, and makes it whole; therefore the two omentum-spits are of k─Бrshmarya wood.

Eggeling
  1. He cuts it (the omentum) off on all sides (from the belly) and heats it at the cooking-fire: thus it becomes cooked for him already at this (fire) 16. The Agn─лdh again takes a firebrand (from the ┼Ъ─Бmitra, and walks in front). They go behind the pit (c─Бtv─Бla) and proceed to the ─Аhavan─лya. The Adhvaryu throws that (top part of the) grass-stalk into the ─Аhavan─лya with, ‘O V─Бyu, graciously accept the drops!’ for this is the kindler (samidh) of the drops 17.

рдЕрдереЛрддреНрддрд░рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ 18 ред рдПрддрддреН рдЙрддреНрддрд░рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рддрдкрдирдореН, рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ рддрдкрдирдВ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рддрдкрдирд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рддреБрд░рдЧреНрдиреНрдпрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдордГ, рддрддреНрд╕рдорд╛рдзрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее резреп рее

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he heats the omentum while standing on the north side; for he is about to pass by the fire and to roast (the omentum) after walking round to the south side. Hereby then he propitiates it, and thus that fire does not injure him while passing by; this is why he heats the omentum while standing on the north side.

рддрджреНрдпс│ШрддреНрд╕рдос│Шрдпрд╛ рди рд╣с│Шрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЗс│Шрдирд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛с│Шрдирд┐ рд╣рд╡реАс│Шс│лрдБс│нрд╖рд┐ рд╣с│Шрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рдиреЗрджс│Шрд╢реГрддрдпрд╛ рд╕рдос│Шрдпрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВс│Ш рдкреНрд░рд╕с│ШрдЬрд╛рдореЗс│Шрддрд┐ рдпс│ШрджреБ рдмрд╛с│Шрд╣реНрдпреЗрди рди рд╣с│Шрд░рдиреНрддреНрдпс│ШрдЧреНрд░реЗрдг рдпреВс│ШрдкрдВ рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛с│Ш рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛с│ШрддреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрд╕реНрддс│Шрд╕реНрдорд╛рджс│ШрдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рдпреВс│ШрдкрдВ рдЪрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ[[!!]] рдЪ рд╣рд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрддрдГс│Ш рдкрд░реАс│ШрддреНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рддрд╛с│Ш рд╢реНрд░рдкрдпрддрд┐рее

рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рддрд╛рдкреЛрдкрдЧрдордирдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрд┐- рддрд╛рдордиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рдпреВрдкрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рддрджреНрдпрджрд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕рдордпрд╛’ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ, рд╡реЗрджрд┐рдордзреНрдпрджреЗрд╢реЗ ‘рди рд╣рд░рдиреНрддрд┐’ ред рдХреЗрдирд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпреЗрдг ? рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╢реЛрд╕реНрддрдпрд╛ ‘рд╡рдкрдпрд╛’ ‘рд╕рдордпрд╛’ рд╕рд╛рдореНрдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрдиреИрд╡ рд╕рд╛рдореАрдкреНрдпреЗрди ‘рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН’ рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпреЗрдиреИрд╡ ‘рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЬрд╛рдо’ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╕рдВрд░рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрдордГ ‘рдЗрддрд┐’ ред рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрдирдВ рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрдирдореН ред рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреБрд░реЛрджреЗрд╢рддреЛ рд╣рд░рдгреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдпреВрдкрд╛рджреНрдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрди рд╣рд░реЗрддреН; ‘рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреН рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН’ ‘рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛’ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдпреВрдкрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╡рдпрд╡рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЙрддреНрддрд░рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрдкрдирдордзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдХрд░реНрддреГрдХрдореН; рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрд╛рддреН рее реиреж рее

Eggeling
  1. They take it along between the sacrificial stake and the fire. The reason why they do not take it across the middle (of the altar) 19, where they take other sacrificial dishes, is lest they should bring the sacrifice in the middle into contact with the uncooked (omentum). And why they do not take it there outside (the altar) along the front of the sacrificial stake, is that they would thereby put it outside the sacrifice; therefore they take it along

between the sacrificial stake and the fire. Having gone round to the south side, the Pratiprasth─Бtr╠е roasts it.

рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБс│Шрд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛с│Шрдорднрд┐с│ШрдЬреБрд╣реЛрддреНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛с│ШрдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡реЗрддреБ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣реЗс│Шрддрд┐ рддс│ШрдереЛ рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдпреИрддреЗс│Ш рд╕реНрддреЛрдХрд╛рдГс│Ш рд╢реГрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛с│Шрд╣рд╛рдХреГрддрд╛ рдЖс│Шрд╣реБрддрдпреЛ рднреВреЧрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН рдкреНрд░рд╛с│ШрдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕реНрд░реБрд╡реЗрдгреЛрдкрд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ 20 ред рддрдерд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рддреНрд░рд╛ рд╡рдкрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рддрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд░реБрд╡реЗрдгрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореБрдкрд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рдп рд╡рдкреЛрдкрд░рд┐ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрд░реНрдЬреБрд╣реБрдпрд╛рддреН тАЬрдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡реЗрддреБ" рдЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдЖрдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп’ рдЖрдЬреНрдпрдВ ‘рд╡реЗрддреБ’ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддреБ, ‘рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛’ рдЗрджрдВ рд╕реБрд╣реБрддрдорд╕реНрддреБ ред рддрдереЛ рд╣реЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ред ‘рдЕрд╕реНрдп’ рд╡рдкрд╛рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп, рд╡рдкрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдкрд╢реЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ ред “рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╖рдЯреНрдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╜рдиреНрдирдВ рд╣реВрдпрддреЗ”- (рдР. рдмреНрд░рд╛. реи реи-рей) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ‘рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдХреГрддрд╛рдГ’ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рджрддреНрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ ‘рдЖрд╣реБрддрдпрдГ’ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее реирез рее

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon the Adhvaryu, having taken ghee with the dipping-spoon, pours it upon the omentum, with, ‘May Agni graciously accept the ghee, Hail!’ Thus those drops thereof reach the fire after becoming cooked offerings, made with Sv─Бh─Б (hail)!

Eggeling
  1. He then says (to the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa 21), ‘Recite to the drops!’ He recites to the drops verses addressed to Agni 22. The reason why he recites to the drops verses addressed to Agni, is that rain originates from gifts made from this earth, for from here it is that Agni obtains the rain; by means of these drops (falling from the omentum) he obtains those (rain) drops, and those drops rain down; therefore he recites to the drops verses addressed to Agni. (рддреНрдпс│Ш) рдЕс│Шрде рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡рдГ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпс│ШрдореЗрд╡рд╛с│ШрдЧреНрд░реЗ рд╜рднрд┐с│ШрдШрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГс│Ш рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорд┐с│Шрддрд┐ рд╡реНрд╡с│ШрджрдиреНрддрд╕реНрддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдпрд╛с│ШрдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдВ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рдиреБрд╡реНрдпрд╛с│ШрдЬрд╣рд╛рд░реИрд╡рдВс│Ш рдХреБрд░реНрд╡реНрд╡с│ШрдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛с│Ш рд╜рдЕрдпс│ШрдордиреНрддс│Шрд░рдЧрд╛рджрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГс│Ш рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгс│Ш рдПрдис│лрдВс│н рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдпрддреАс│Шрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╢реНрд░реАрдзрд░рд╛рджрд┐

(рддреНрдпс│Ш) рдЕс│Шрде рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡рдГ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпс│ШрдореЗрд╡рд╛с│ШрдЧреНрд░реЗ рд╜рднрд┐с│ШрдШрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГс│Ш рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорд┐с│Шрддрд┐ рд╡реНрд╡с│ШрджрдиреНрддрд╕реНрддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдпрд╛с│ШрдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдВ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рдиреБрд╡реНрдпрд╛с│ШрдЬрд╣рд╛рд░реИрд╡рдВс│Ш рдХреБрд░реНрд╡реНрд╡с│ШрдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛с│Ш рд╜рдЕрдпс│ШрдордиреНрддс│Шрд░рдЧрд╛рджрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГс│Ш рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгс│Ш рдПрдис│лрдВс│н рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдпрддреАс│Шрддрд┐рее

рд╣реБрддреНрд╡рд╛с│Ш рд╡рдкрд╛с│ШрдореЗрд╡рд╛с│ШрдЧреНрд░реЗ рд╜рднрд┐рдШрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐рее
рдЕс│Шрде рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рдГ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпс│ШрдореЗрд╡рд╛с│ШрдЧреНрд░реЗ рд╜рднрд┐с│ШрдШрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГс│Ш рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорд┐с│Шрддрд┐ рд╡с│ШрджрдиреНрддрд╕реНрддс│ШрджреБ рд╣ рдпрд╛с│ШрдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдВ рдЪс│Шрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрд░рдиреБрд╡реНрдпрд╛с│ШрдЬрд╣рд╛рд░реИрд╡рдВс│Ш рдХреБрд░реНрд╡с│ШрдиреНрддрдореН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛с│Ш рдЕрдпс│ШрдордиреНрддс│Шрд░рдЧрд╛рджрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГс│Ш рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгс│Ш рдПрдис│лрдВ рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдпрддреАс│Шрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рд╣реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рдкрд╛рдореЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ 26 ред рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпрдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдЬрдВ рд╣реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ ‘рдЕрдЧреНрд░реЗ’ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреН ‘рд╡рдкрд╛рдореЗрд╡’ рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдЬрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рднрд┐рдШрд╛рд░рдпреЗрддреН ред ‘рдЕрде’ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН рдЕрдиреВрдпрд╛рдЬрд╛рджреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ ‘рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореН’ ред рдЪрд░рдХрд╢рд╛рдЦреЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╜рд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд░рдГ ‘рдЪрд░рдХрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрд╡рд╡рдГ’ ред ‘рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореЗрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд░реЗ рд╜рднрд┐рдШрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐’ ред рджрдзрд┐рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рдорд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╡рддреН рдЧрд╡рд╛рдордиреНрддрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН; рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ, рддрджреНрдзреЗрддреБрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрддреНрд╡рдореН ред ‘рддрджреБ’ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирднрд┐рдШрд╛рд░рдгрдкреНрд░рд╛рдердореНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ тАШрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдореН’ ‘рдЕрдиреБ’ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпреАрдХреГрддреНрдп ‘рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЬрд╣рд╛рд░’ рдЙрдХреНрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдЕрдиреБрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЬрд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рд╢рд╛рдкрдГ ред рдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рдирд╖реНрдЯрд┐- рдПрд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореНрдп рд╡рдкрд╛рдореЗрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рд╡рднрд┐рдШрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрдореН ‘рдЕрдпрдордзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГ’ рдкреГрд╖рджрд╛рдЬреНрдпрдорддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдордиреН ‘рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдВ’ рдЦрд▓реБ ‘рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рдЧрд╛рддреН’ рдЕрддрдГ ‘рдПрдирдореН’ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдВ ‘рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛ рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдпрддрд┐’- ‘рдЗрддрд┐’ рдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд▓реНрдХреНрдпрдВ рд╕рдореНрдмреЛрдзреНрдп рд╡рдХреНрддрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдгреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рд╣ рее реирек рее

Eggeling
  1. Having offered, he bastes first the omentum, then the clotted ghee. Now the Karaka-Adhvaryus, forsooth, baste first the clotted ghee, arguing that the clotted ghee is the breath; and a Caraka-Adhvaryu, forsooth, cursed Y─Бj├▒avalkya for so doing, saying, ‘That Adhvaryu has shut out the breath; the breath shall depart from him!’

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

Eggeling
  1. But he, looking at his arms, said, ‘These hoary arms–what in the world has become of the Br─Бhman’s word 27!’ Let him not heed that (objection of the Karakas); for this is the last fore-offering,–and this being a havis-offering, at the last fore-offering he first pours ghee into the dhruv─Б, being about to offer the first two butter-portions with it 28. Now, on the present occasion, he will first offer the omentum; therefore let him first baste the omentum, then the clotted ghee. And though he does not baste the victim with ghee, ’lest he should baste the uncooked,’ that whole victim of his yet becomes (as it were) basted with ghee in that he bastes the omentum; let him therefore first baste the omentum, then the clotted ghee.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he makes an ‘underlayer’ of ghee (in the juh┼л-spoon), and lays a piece of gold thereon. Then, cutting off the omentum (from the spits and putting it into the spoon), he says (to the Hotr╠е), ‘Recite (the invitatory prayer) to Agni and Soma

for the omentum and fat of the buck!’ He then lays (another) piece of gold on (the omentum) and bastes it twice with ghee above.

Eggeling
  1. The reason why there is a piece of gold on both sides is this. When they offer the victim in the fire they slay it; and gold means immortal life: hence it (the victim) rests in immortal life. And so it rises from hence, and so it lives; for this reason there is a piece of gold 31 on both sides. Having called for the ┼Ъraushaс╣н, he says (to the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa), ‘Prompt (the Hotr╠е to recite the offering-prayer 32 on) the omentum and fat of the buck for Agni and Soma!’ He does not say, ‘. . . (the omentum and fat) brought forward;’ when the Soma has been pressed he says, ‘brought forward 33.’ He offers when the Vashaс╣н has been pronounced.

Eggeling
  1. Having offered the omentum, he lays the two spits together and throws them after (the omentum into the fire), with, ‘Consecrated by Sv─Бh─Б, go ye to ┼кrdhvanabhas 34, son of the Maruts!’ He does so, thinking, ‘Lest these two wherewith we have cooked the omentum should come to nought.’

Eggeling
  1. The reason why they perform with the omen-tum is this. For whatever deity the victim is seized, that same deity he pleases by means of that fat (part); and that same deity, thus pleased with that fat, waits

patiently for the other sacrificial dishes being cooked; this is why they perform with the omentum.

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рд╜рд╖реНрдЯрдорд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (рей-рео-реи)

Eggeling
  1. They then cleanse themselves over the pit 36. For in quieting and cutting up (the victim) they wound it; and water being a means of soothing, they now soothe it by means of water, heal it by means of water; therefore they cleanse themselves over the pit.
